International News 67

British Airship's Successful Atlantic Voyage

Reuters, London, 1st: The voyage record of the British airship R100 to Montreal has now been published. The voyage was initially very quiet. The people on board passed the time by playing card games and sleeping. Everyone was able to maintain the temperature without using the electric heaters in the cabins. Outside Father Point on the St. Lawrence River, a defect was first discovered in the left wing. Later, the airship encountered thunderstorms, which disturbed the air, and the right wing was also slightly damaged. Apart from this, the airship had no problems at all. The airship flew in the sky for 79 hours, eight of which were due to wing damage. The crew did an excellent job of repairing the damage. After the airship landed, there were still five tons of oil remaining.

Important News

○ 103rd Meeting of the Legislative Yuan: The Legislative Yuan held its 103rd meeting at 8:00 AM today (August 2nd). The following members were present: Lü Zhiyi, Shi Shangkuan, Jiao Yitang, Chen Zhaoying, Lin Bin, Dai Xiujun, Tao Xuan, Shao Yuanchong, Zhao Shibei, Enke Batu, Sun Jingya, Niu Yongjian, Lou Tongsun, Wu Shangying, Zhang Zhihan, Wang Yongbin, Cai Xuan, Liu Guanxun, Lu Zhonglin, Liu Jixue, Luo Ding, Deng Zhaoyin, Zhang Fengjiu, Fu Bingchang, Chen Changheng, Wang Baozhen, Zhu Hezhong, Lu Yi Nong, Liu Jingxin, Zheng Kaichen, and 30 others. Hu Hanmin presided over the meeting. The following matters were discussed: (1) Review of the Draft Law on Fortified Zones: It was resolved to submit the draft to the Land Law Drafting Committee for review. (2) The 86th National Government meeting regarding the Executive Yuan's submission of a request from the Capital Police Department to amend Article 8 of the Enforcement Rules of the Trade Union Law: It was resolved to submit the draft to the Trade Union Law Drafting Committee for review. (3) Review of the Supplementary Agreement and Ratification Documents to the Sino-Polish Treaty of Friendship, Commerce and Navigation: It was resolved to submit the documents to the Foreign Affairs Committee for review. (4) The Business Law Drafting Committee of the Legislative Yuan reported on the Executive Yuan's response to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's submission regarding whether there is a clear provision in the Law on Joint Associations of Industrial Organizations above one area that allows for the separate formulation of regulations, or whether the law should be revised as appropriate: It was resolved to amend and pass the law. (5) Review of the Draft Enforcement Rules of the Examination Law: It was resolved to submit the draft to the French Law Committee for review. (6) Review of the Draft Examination Regulations (7) Review of the Draft Associate Examiner Regulations (8) Review of the Draft Proctoring Regulations: It was resolved to submit the draft to the Legislative Committee for review.

Attached is the amendment to the Trade Association Law: An article is added after the original Article 13 and listed as Article 14. The text of Article 14 is as follows: (Article 14) Two or more trade associations may form a joint association with the consent of more than two-thirds of their members. The articles of association of the aforementioned joint industrial and commercial associations that belong to the same province shall be approved by the provincial government and submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for record. Those that do not belong to the same province or that cross provinces and cities directly under the Executive Yuan shall be approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The joint association of industrial and commercial associations is subject to the supervision of the local administrative authorities where its office is located. Except for the provisions of the preceding three paragraphs, the provisions on trade associations in the Third Meeting shall apply mutatis mutandis to the joint association of industrial and commercial associations.

Martial Law Declared in Hankou 68

Hankou Correspondence: The Wuhan Military Camp believes that the security of the rear is of utmost importance during this period of military operations. It has ordered the Wuhan Garrison Headquarters to strictly enforce martial law. In addition to the Wuchang and Hanyang districts, which have already been ordered by the Headquarters to cut off traffic after 12:00 AM every night, the Hankou district will also officially declare martial law starting today (August 1st). The Garrison Headquarters' notice is recorded below: (1) Wuhan is an important town on the Yangtze River, and it is also a time of military operations. According to the order of the Commander-in-Chief of the Wuhan Military Camp, martial law will be enforced in the Wuhan Garrison Area. In addition to the fact that Hankou is a special commercial field and martial law is being carried out covertly, traffic in the Wuchang and Hanyang districts is completely cut off from 12:00 AM every night until dawn the next morning, etc., and has been specifically ordered to be followed. Subsequently, at the 16th meeting of this Headquarters on July 29th, after proposals and endorsements from various garrison agencies and troops, it was resolved that the entire Hankou district should be requested to follow the example of Wuchang and Hanyang districts and completely cut off traffic from 12:00 AM every night until dawn the next day. This Headquarters has submitted a document to the Commander-in-Chief of the Wuhan Military Camp for review and approval, and has now received instructions stating that it has been approved. Starting from August 1st, traffic in the Hankou district during the martial law period will be completely cut off from 12:00 AM every night until dawn the next morning. The area around Liujiamiao Jiang'an and the area around the German-Chinese School and the upper street of Qiaokou will be cut off from traffic from 9:00 PM every night until dawn the next morning. Soldiers and officers who are traveling on official business must display the license plates or flags of their respective agencies or troops on the front of their vehicles, and when approaching guard posts, they must slow down, stop their vehicles, and only be allowed to pass after the guard post soldier or police officer has answered the password correctly or has inspected and verified the pass. In addition to issuing a notice to be strictly enforced in compliance, a notice is hereby issued for the military, civilians, and others to abide by it. (2) It is found that the variety of amusement venues is complex. Even with close supervision during peacetime, it is easy to cause trouble. During martial law, it is even more inappropriate to open night markets that gather thousands or even tens of thousands of people in one place. It is easier for bandits to hide in the chaos, making it more difficult to prevent and investigate. This Headquarters bears the full responsibility for garrisoning the area and should take precautions in advance in order to ensure thorough planning and security. A notice is hereby issued to all managers of the amusement venues to comply with the order that night markets are not allowed to open until martial law is declared lifted. Anyone who dares to deliberately violate the order will be arrested and prosecuted. (August 1st)

Recent News from Jiangxi Province Regarding Communist Bandits 69

Situation of Martial Law in the Provincial Capital

A Nanchang dispatch states that when the 18th Division's 52nd and 54th Brigades recovered Xingan and Zhangshu, Huang Gonglüe, Luo Binghui, and others split into two routes and fled. One route fled along the east bank of the Gan River towards Le'an in Fuzhou, while the other fled west across the Gan River to Gao'an. However, Gao'an is only 120 *li* from the provincial capital and only has a small number of Peace Preservation Corps troops. As a result, on the evening of the 26th, the county seat fell to the bandits. Commander-in-Chief Lu and Division Commander Zhang, upon receiving the news, immediately telegraphed the 52nd Brigade to pursue towards Gao'an from Zhangshu. They also transferred the 107th Regiment of the 54th Brigade back to the provincial capital from Zhangshu, which then took small boats across the Gan River to Shengmi to advance towards Gao'an and suppress the bandits. At the same time, the Municipal Public Security Bureau also ordered the Second Security Team to station themselves at Wanshou Palace, 30 *li* from the city (a necessary route from the provincial capital to Gao'an), to provide defense. According to reconnaissance reports yesterday, the bandits in Gao'an actually only number slightly over a thousand, but they are making a false show of strength, claiming to be 20,000 strong. Yesterday, the bandits held a meeting in Gao'an to kidnap and extort ransoms. In the provincial capital, since the loss of Gao'an, people have become more anxious than on the 24th and 25th. In reality, the defensive works, electric fences, and trenches around the city are extremely solid, making it impossible for the bandits to fly across. Commander-in-Chief Lu reported at the provincial government's weekly memorial service yesterday: "All important places are garrisoned with heavy troops, and the security of Nanchang can be absolutely guaranteed. I hope the citizens can rest assured. As for the defensive works of the provincial capital, they are extremely thorough. Only a small number of soldiers are needed to defend them, and the majority can be drawn to the front lines to suppress the bandits. The communists are all a bunch of rabble. Peng Dehuai was a stable boy under former Independent Fifth Division Commander Zhou. Zhu De is a disgruntled military man. The so-called Chairman Mao Zedong of the Communist Military Commission is a normal school graduate. He once said to people in Guangdong, 'I only need 20,000 or 30,000 yuan and I will not revolt.' How can such an idea be considered revolutionary? It would be a real joke if we were frightened by this bunch of people." At the moment, the provincial capital has issued a proclamation strictly prohibiting the fabrication of rumors and the creation of disturbances. All amusement parks in the city have been uniformly closed for business. From 10:00 PM every night to 5:00 AM the next morning, all traffic is completely cut off, and no one is allowed to pass without a special pass. In order to unify propaganda, the Martial Law Headquarters held a meeting of reporters from various newspapers in the city yesterday to report on the reasons for this martial law and to establish a news censorship office to inspect all news items. All newspaper reporters were issued passes to facilitate their movement. It has just been reported that Li Baobing's brigade, sent by Director He to Jiangxi for joint defense, has already arrived in Jiujiang. The 52nd and 54th Brigades, which set out from the province to Gao'an, have arrived in the Shengmi and Wanshou Palace area. After hearing the news, the communist bandits in that area are extorting everywhere, preparing to flee elsewhere. At the same time, Fengxin is also sending an urgent plea to the provincial authorities, but it is unknown if it is the same group. (July 29th)

○The Lower Reaches of the Yellow River in Shandong Have Emerged from Dangerous Works; Puyang is Also Reporting an Emergency

A Jinan dispatch states that since the beginning of the *fu* period this year, continuous torrential rains have created a situation of flooding. The Shandong River Affairs Bureau has recently received repeated reports of dangerous works from upstream and downstream. According to a report from the Luokou section, as of yesterday (the 27th), the water level continues to rise and has now risen to 9.4 *zhang* above sea level, with a continued rising trend. The danger line at that location is 9.3 *zhang*, and the water is only 0.26 *zhang* below that level. If the current situation can be maintained during the day, Jinan will not experience dangerous works. However, dangerous works have already emerged on the north and south banks of the downstream. According to a report from the River Affairs Bureau as of the 26th, there are four locations reporting dangerous works: Wang Wangzhuang in Putai County and Fengjia on the south bank, and Sunjia in Lijin County and Wang Zaojia in Huimin County on the north bank. Li Guojun, director of the River Affairs Bureau, recently requested the provincial government to allocate funds for rush repairs during the *fu* period. Deng Chongxi proposed a discussion at the first provincial affairs meeting, and it was decided to provisionally allocate 120,000 yuan to be shared by the 59 counties along the river. However, this amount cannot be fully disbursed at once, so the River Affairs Bureau consulted with the Finance Department to have the bureau raise the funds and the department reimburse them to meet the urgent need. The River Affairs Bureau has now borrowed 20,000 yuan from the Bank of China and 10,000 yuan from the High Court and will immediately distribute them to facilitate the rush repairs. As for the upstream, there are no dangerous works in this province, but the Liuzhuang stone dam in Hebei Province has experienced dangerous works. The construction there is in Hebei, but the harm is in Shandong. There are a total of twelve stone dams in Liuzhuang, and the tenth and eleventh dams have experienced dangerous works and are in a very critical state. The Puyang County government recently telegraphed the Shandong River Affairs Bureau to report this and requested an allocation of 240,000 yuan of funds borne by Shandong to meet the urgent need. According to previous decisions by the provincial government regarding the special river works at the Liuzhuang stone dam, Shandong Province would provide 240,000 yuan annually, with 120,000 yuan borne by the provincial treasury and 120,000 yuan borne by the eight counties of Caozhou, with the River Works Committee overseeing the completion. After the changes in Jinan, no one is responsible for the River Works Committee, and the funds are also without source. After receiving the urgent telegram from Puyang County, Li Guojun, director of the River Affairs Bureau, immediately telegraphed this situation to the Hebei River Affairs Bureau, requesting urgent measures for rush repairs. The Shandong funds will be discussed further. (July 28th)

Anti-Banditry Conference Convened in Anhui Province 70

A Bengbu dispatch states that Wei Lihuang, commander of the Anhui Provincial Bandit Suppression, convened a provincial anti-banditry conference in Bengbu, attended by the county magistrates of sixty counties and the commanders of seven bandit suppression zones, in order to eliminate banditry and alleviate the suffering of the people in northern and southern Anhui due to the rampant communist bandits. The meeting was held at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 1st in the general office of the Bandit Suppression Headquarters in Tangwei. Attendees included Liu Wenming, deputy director of the Provincial Security Department; Xu Huanting, chief of staff of the New Fifth Brigade; Chen Jincheng, representative of the Independent Fifteenth Brigade; Ji Rongzhen, representative of the Third Cavalry Brigade; Chen Guojun, chief of staff of the Bandit Suppression Headquarters; Zhu Ding, director of the General Staff Office; Bao Kai, magistrate of Bo County; Zhou Farong, representative of Fengyang County; and over forty others. Wei Lihuang was absent due to a trip to Xuzhou, and Chief of Staff Chen chaired the meeting. First, Chen delivered an opening speech, followed by Zhu Ding, who reported on the reasons for convening the anti-banditry conference. Liu Wenming reported on the situation of the communist bandits in Anhui Province. The county magistrates and representatives successively reported on the bandit situation in their respective counties. Then, the participants discussed the Provisional Regulations for Bandit Suppression in Anhui Province and the Outline of the Bandit Suppression Plan, totaling 23 articles each, all of which were passed. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 PM and continued at 2:00 PM in the afternoon to discuss the proposals of the various counties. The results were as follows: (1) The proposal to implement the collective responsibility system for bandit suppression (proposed by Mengcheng, Yingshang, Guoyang, and Langxi Counties) was resolved to be implemented during the bandit suppression period according to the collective responsibility system. (2) The proposal for joint defense and patrols among the counties (proposed by Mengcheng and Liu'an) was resolved to be effectively stipulated by the district commanders. (3) The proposal to prohibit miscellaneous troops from recruiting old units was resolved to comply with the commander-in-chief's order that in the future, regardless of which unit recruits old units in the bandit suppression area, any behavior exceeding the bounds of propriety should be dealt with at their discretion. The county magistrates and commanders should investigate any such behavior and report it to the Provincial Bandit Suppression Headquarters for verification. (4) The proposal that all military and commercial vehicles passing through garrisoned troops, security corps, or patrol teams must be inspected (proposed by Mengcheng) was resolved to be implemented in the bandit suppression area. (5) The proposal for unified command (proposed by Mengcheng) was resolved to be delegated to the district bandit suppression commanders. (6) The proposal that if bandits from County A are captured by bandit suppression troops from County B within the territory of County A, they should be handed over to County A for verification (proposed by Mengcheng County) was resolved to be passed. (7) The proposal to request the appointment of the county magistrates of each county as military judges of the headquarters (proposed by Wuhu and Guoyang) was resolved to be handled after the headquarters' regulations on the trial of bandit cases are stipulated. (8) The proposal to delineate districts and clear the countryside to eliminate the source of bandits (proposed by Wuhu County) was resolved to be handled during the clearing of the countryside. (9) The proposal to thoroughly reorganize the people's self-defense forces in each county (proposed by Liu'an and Fuyang) was resolved to be passed. (10) The proposal for the counties to jointly build gas-powered vehicle roads (proposed by Yingshang, Fuyang, and Liu'an) was resolved to be ordered by the bandit suppression headquarters to each county to jointly build them simultaneously. (11) The proposal regarding opinions on the 15th Brigade's bandit suppression zone (proposed by the 15th Brigade, intending to be responsible for the area along the river, including Guichi, Tongling, Datong, and Wuhu) was resolved to be handled in accordance with the bandit suppression zones divided by the bandit suppression headquarters. (12) The proposal regarding propaganda methods (proposed by the 15th Brigade) was resolved to be handled by the district commanders and county magistrates of each district. (13) The proposal to replenish the counties with ammunition (proposed by Guoyang) was resolved to have each county investigate the types and quantities of ammunition needed and report them to the bandit suppression headquarters for purchase. (14) The proposal to rigorously implement self-defense registration to facilitate the clearing of the countryside (proposed by Fuyang) was resolved to be handled during the clearing of the countryside. After the discussion, a photograph was taken, and the meeting adjourned. (August 1st)

Anti-Banditry Conference in the Eight Counties of Xuzhou 71

A Xuzhou dispatch states that Song Runtian, the Xuzhou Garrison Commander, convened an anti-banditry conference in the Garrison Headquarters at the Garden Hotel on the 31st, after being ordered to concurrently serve as the anti-banditry commander of the eight counties, and invited representatives from the eight counties to attend. The meeting began at 1:00 PM, and attendees included Yang Weifeng, magistrate of Tongshan County; Fang Qingping, representative of Feng County; Zheng Yunqiao, representative of Su County; Wang Enpu, representative of Yangshan; Liu Guorong, Ding Jishi, and Zhu Bichen, representatives of Suining; Jiang Quansheng, representative of Suqian; Luo Yuanye, magistrate of Pi County, etc. The representative of Pei County was absent. Miao Zhensong, chief of staff of the Garrison Headquarters, and Meng Hongsheng, secretary, were also present. Commander Song chaired the meeting. First, Song reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that he hoped that the counties would work together to clear out bandits, and that the communist party was manipulating the bandits. If the bandits are defeated, the communists would also be defeated. The following twelve items were discussed and resolved: (1) Each county should report the number of districts, the number of militia firearms in each district, and the overall current defense situation in detail (2) Each county should report the organization, strength, and number of firearms in the police force, as well as the deployment situation in detail. (3) Each county should submit a list of the names, ranks, and seals of the county magistrate, public security bureau chief, police brigade commander, and district chiefs. (4) Each county should report the bandit-producing areas, villages, and towns, as well as the names and numbers of the bandit leaders and bandits in detail. (The above information will be provided in forms prepared by the headquarters.) (5) If small-scale bandit incidents occur in any district of each county, the district chief should convene the members of the local militia to be responsible for suppressing them. If the strength is insufficient, they may join forces with neighboring districts to assist in the suppression and report it to the county magistrate. (6) If banditry occurs simultaneously in several districts of each county, the district chiefs should jointly be responsible for suppressing them. The county magistrate may also send a police team to assist in the encirclement and suppression, but false reports should not be made to avoid wasting military force. (7) Regarding passwords and signals, the headquarters will stipulate and issue them, and the flags and armbands will be designed by the headquarters, and each county will manufacture them for its own use (but only for use during bandit suppression). (8) Regarding rewards and punishments for those who contribute to bandit suppression, if there are extraordinary contributions, the county magistrate may report them to the headquarters for submission to the higher authorities for rewards, subject to approval. (The regulations on rewards for captured firearms and ammunition will be announced separately.) (9) The methods of compensation for officers and soldiers killed or wounded in bandit suppression will follow the peacetime compensation regulations promulgated by the central government. (10) The expenses for the establishment and operation of the joint office, public funds, and food expenses for office staff will be prepared by each county and approved by the meeting. (11) In addition to the representative from each county in Xuzhou stationed in Xuzhou, the office should have a clerk, two scribes, and messengers. Salaries should be stipulated and paid monthly. (The above two items will be coordinated by the headquarters.) (12) Each representative will hold a regular meeting once a week. If special circumstances occur, meetings may be convened at any time. Finally, Secretary Meng suggested establishing joint bandit suppression regulations for implementation. The meeting adjourned at 3:00 PM, and the representatives returned to their respective counties. (July 31st)

○Methods for Promoting Financial Bonds in Guangdong Province; Unredeemed Banknotes Will Also Be Redeemed

A Guangzhou dispatch states that since Guangdong Province decided to issue 15 million yuan in financial treasury bonds, the Department of Finance has recently formulated methods for promoting sales. Once issued, over 5 million yuan in unredeemed banknotes can be recovered in August and September, and a certain type of unredeemed banknote can be redeemed in the third month. An investigation of the promotional procedures and budget is as follows: (A) The allocation method is divided into four items: (1) Sales allocated to wealthy households in each county. (2) Sales allocated to Guangzhou, Shantou, and stores in other cities that have previously obtained business licenses, at 3% of the business license capital. Commercial banks and silver firms are allocated at 5%. (3) Sales allocated to shops in Guangzhou and Shantou based on one month's rent. (4) Sales allocated to contractors of *li*, tax, and donation revenue under the Department of Finance based on half a month's worth of their payment amount. (B) The sales-linking method is divided into three items: (1) For merchants paying national and provincial taxes, as well as *li*, tax, and donation revenue in counties and cities, 20% of the tax amount is linked to sales. (2) Twenty percent of the fines from the judicial, administrative, and national tax agencies of Guangdong Province are linked to sales. (3) Twenty percent of the daily expenses of national, provincial, and municipal schools under the judicial, administrative, and national tax agencies of Guangdong Province are linked to the monthly budget. All of the above items, except for sales-linking methods two and three, which are unrelated to the central government's banknotes, can use central government banknotes to pay in installments based on the order of payment, at the following rates: 50% for payments made in August 19, 30% for payments made in September, and 20% for payments made in October. An investigation of the allocation method shows that it is limited to two months for the full amount to be raised. Therefore, averaging the payment of central government banknotes at 40%, the second category of the allocation method, commercial licenses, is estimated to be allocated approximately 3 million yuan based on an average of 4% of the capital amount. Using 40% of central government banknotes, approximately 1 million yuan in central government banknotes is required. The third category, rent, is allocated approximately 800,000 to 900,000 yuan, requiring approximately 300,000 yuan in central government banknotes when calculated at 40%. The fourth category, half a month's worth of revenue for each contractor, can be allocated approximately 1 million yuan, requiring approximately 700,000 to 800,000 yuan in central government banknotes when calculated at 50%. Furthermore, the first category of the sales-linking method, various taxes in the provinces and cities, will link sales at 20% of the tax amount and require approximately 800,000 yuan in central government banknotes each month. In addition, the first category of the allocation method will allocate sales to wealthy households in each county, and using an average payment of 40% in central government banknotes, the amount required will be significant, estimated at approximately 5 million yuan in central government banknotes between August and September. Based on the actual calculation of supply and demand, the market price of central government banknotes can rise to over 90%. At the same time, the Department of Finance will take the opportunity to devise a way to first redeem a certain type of unredeemed banknote. (July 28th)

Civil Law 72

Preliminary Points for the Chapters on Inheritance and Family (Continued) Opinions of the Central Political Council's Review

(2) Preliminary Points for Family Law: Point 1: Classification of Relatives. Relatives should be divided into three categories: spouse, blood relatives, and relatives by marriage. (Explanation: The old laws of our country divided relatives into clan relatives, maternal relatives, and marital relatives, which originated from the clan system. It is necessary to make a fundamental reform in the current situation. The occurrence of kinship is based on either blood or marriage. Therefore, the classification of relatives should be defined as three categories: spouse, blood relatives, and relatives by marriage. Blood relatives and relatives by marriage should be further divided into lineal and collateral relatives. This classification is not only natural but also in line with the legal systems of the world. Point 2: Surnames between spouses and children: (1) As a principle, the wife should adopt the husband's surname, and the husband should adopt the wife's surname when entering her family as a son-in-law, but exceptions may be provided. (2) Children take their father's surname. (3) Children of a son-in-law take their mother's surname, but exceptions may be provided. (Explanation) This problem can be assumed to be the following six options, and their strengths and weaknesses can be studied: (1) Both spouses use an agreed-upon surname (the husband's surname, the wife's surname, or a third surname), and the children follow suit. (2) Both spouses use their own surnames, and the children combine the surnames of both parents. (3) Both spouses use their own surnames, the sons take the father's surname, and the daughters take the mother's surname. (4) The wife takes the husband's surname, and the children take the father's surname. (5) The husband takes the wife's surname, and the children take the mother's surname. (6) The wife adopts the husband's surname, and the children take the father's surname. The first, second, and third options are in line with the principle of gender equality, which is their strength. However, if the first option is used, spouses have the freedom to choose a surname, and children also have this freedom when they marry, which may result in frequent changes of surname. Then, the reason for having a surname is only superficial, which is its weakness. If the second option is used, it is not impossible for children to combine two surnames, but the children of children will have more than two characters in their surname, and the number of characters will increase with each generation without limit. This is also its weakness. If the third option is used, the surnames of brothers and sisters will be different, which is somewhat strange, which is its weakness. The fourth option, where the wife does not retain her own surname but takes the husband's surname entirely, seems somewhat biased. The fifth option is equally biased and is not advisable. In the sixth option, the wife can retain her own surname, and the husband will not change his surname. In practice, it seems easier to implement. As for the surname of the children, since there is no other perfect solution, it is proposed to continue to follow the father's surname. However, this refers to the situation where the wife marries into the husband's family. If the husband enters the wife's family as a son-in-law, the husband will adopt the wife's surname, and the children will also follow the mother's surname to show some intention of gender equality. Therefore, it is proposed to set this as the principle. Whether to set another exception (for example, if the spouses have another agreement) can be discussed at length by those responsible for drafting the provisions. In general, there is no perfect solution to achieve complete gender equality in this matter, as mentioned above. Since gender equality is difficult to achieve perfectly, other forms of equality, such as economic equality, political power equality, and private rights equality, should not be pursued in vain. If it is necessary to make the surnames perfectly equal, it is very difficult. However, within the possible scope, it should aim to comply with the principle of equality. Point 3: Scope of Relatives. The scope of relatives should not be specified, but the definition of relatives and the method of calculating degrees of kinship should be specified. (Explanation) The relationship between humans giving rise to kinship has a distinction between blood relatives and relatives by marriage, and the scope of blood relatives and relatives by marriage is originally difficult to determine. In terms of blood relatives, from parents to grandparents and so on, going upwards, and from children to grandchildren and so on, going downwards, there is already a connection of blood. Even if the generations are far apart, it cannot be said that they are not relatives. The same is true for lineal relatives, and also for collateral relatives. In terms of relatives by marriage, there is no fixed scope, just like blood relatives. The scope of relatives stipulated by law is because relatives sometimes have a legal relationship with each other, and in fact, it cannot be unlimited. Therefore, it is stipulated to facilitate application. However, the circumstances of various legal relationships are different, and the scope of the regulations should also vary accordingly. Therefore, even if a general regulation is forcibly made, when encountering special legal relationships, such as the prohibition of marriage between relatives in civil matters, the duty of support between relatives, and the rights of inheritance, and in criminal matters, the aggravation of punishment and kinship relationships, it is still more practical to stipulate their scope separately. Therefore, there is no need to make a general regulation on the scope of relatives. However, since the classification of relatives has been fundamentally reformed and divided into blood relatives and relatives by marriage, it is not easy to understand what their definitions are without clearly defining them in writing. Since blood relatives and relatives by marriage must be distinguished according to their closeness in special legal relationships, it is necessary to calculate their closeness in terms of degrees of kinship. Therefore, the definition of relatives and the method of calculating degrees of kinship should be stipulated. Furthermore, the methods of calculating degrees of kinship are divided into two types: Roman law and monastic law. The method of calculating degrees of kinship in Roman law is to count up and down from oneself in a direct line, with one generation being one degree of kinship. In a collateral line, count from oneself to the person of common origin, and then count down from the person of common origin to the relative in question, with the total number of generations being the number of degrees of kinship. The method of calculating degrees of kinship in monastic law is the same as Roman law for direct relatives, but not for collateral relatives. Count from oneself to the person of common origin, and then count from the relative in question to the person of common origin. For those whose generations are the same, the number of generations on one side is used to determine the degree of kinship. For those whose generations are not the same, the larger number is used to determine the degree of kinship. This is the difference from Roman law. Most countries in the world use Roman law. The calculation of Roman law is based on the distance of blood relation to determine the degree of kinship, which is in line with reason. Monastic law originates from Western religious traditions, and its calculation of degrees of kinship does not fully follow the proportion of closeness. For example, if the number of generations in two lines is different, the larger number is used to determine the degree of kinship, so the line with fewer generations often does not distinguish between superior and inferior and is of the same degree of kinship, which is not reasonable. The reason why our country previously adopted monastic law was because it was relatively similar to the ancient clan mourning system, and all clan relatives within the five degrees of mourning could be covered by the four degrees of kinship under monastic law without omission. Therefore, from the draft of the Civil Law of the Qing Dynasty to the most recent drafts, all have used monastic law to calculate degrees of kinship. Now that the classification of relatives has been fundamentally reformed and divided into two major categories, blood relatives and relatives by marriage, it is no longer related to the so-called mourning system. We should choose the best and change to Roman law. (To be continued)

Wuhu Quick News 73

This year's autumn harvest in the counties of southern Anhui is abundant, and the price of rice is gradually falling, with ordinary rice costing about 13.50 or 13.60 yuan per *shi*. Yesterday, the Wuhu Municipal Office, the Wuhu County Government, the General Chamber of Commerce, and other agencies held a special meeting at the General Chamber of Commerce. It was decided that all four price stabilization bureaus would uniformly cease price stabilization today (the 1st), and the Price Stabilization Committee would also prepare to dissolve.

Yesterday, they received a reply stating that the headquarters attached great importance to Wuhu's security. The Third Battalion is approved to remain in Wuhu, and there are plans to divide and suppress the bandit troubles in Ningguo and Guangde, to consolidate the rear. The bandits who robbed the Huangmu Ferry in Nanling County are still entrenched in the vicinity of the Ma Ren Ferry area and have not fled elsewhere. Yesterday, the Wuhu County Garrison and the nearby militia surrounded and attacked them, and a fierce battle lasted for several hours. The passenger and cargo ships traveling from Nanling to Wuhu were blocked by the shelling. Later, fearing that the authorities would increase reinforcements, the bandits began to flee towards Fanchang. The Nanling shuttle boat only arrived in Wuhu today.

Due to the disagreement among the Jiangsu and Anhui commissioners, the disputes were difficult to resolve. As a result, they are becoming increasingly rampant, and robberies are occurring repeatedly. Recently, the practice of extorting loans has become even more widespread. These people send out dozens of threatening letters every day, delivered by their armed accomplices. At first, they would choose relatively well-off families, but now they extort loans from everyone, regardless of their wealth. Those who are extorted are mostly peaceful farming families who are too busy with plowing to move, so they have no choice but to let them be slaughtered under threat. Some have been extorted several times, resulting in the complete loss of their property. It is especially pitiful. Furthermore, any women who are slightly attractive are often kidnapped by them when passing through bandit dens. As a result, people fear them like tigers.

Songjiang 75

Maple Ridge Bandit Leader Executed: Jin Haiqin, the Maple Ridge area and his family of seven were burned to death by the Communist Party in 1927. The culprit Wang Ziqin was executed last year. There was also a leading bandit named Gu Guilong who escaped and has been wanted with a reward ever since. He was captured in Shengze last month and escorted to Songjiang. After interrogation by the county government, the bandit confessed to being the chairman of the Communist Party, and could not remember the number of kidnapping and murder cases he had committed in order to raise funds and purchase guns. The family members of the victims also identified the bandit in court, and the bandit fully confessed. Even while in hiding, he secretly directed everything, causing the bandit atmosphere in Maple Ridge to be very rampant. Recently, he bought several boxes of guns for 3,500 yuan and distributed them to his followers. His crimes are heinous, and the people of Maple Ridge hate him to the core. The county government received a confidential telegram from the provincial government approving the death penalty and the county government immediately (the 2nd) took the bandit leader Gu Guilong, verified his identity, and tied him to the execution ground at Yu Huang Pavilion for execution by firing squad.

High Court Orders Release of Prisoners: Zhang Peicheng, the county's warden, recently received an order from the High Court that the prisons are overcrowded and must be cleared. Those who have been sentenced to imprisonment for less than one year and have served more than half of their sentence may be released on bail in accordance with the bail regulations. The warden immediately made a list and submitted it for approval.

Farmer Threatened by Bandits: Cai Yisheng, a farmer in the southern part of Xihu Tang, a farmer in the southern part of Xihu Tang, only cultivates dozens of *mu* of rented land and has no savings. One night at the end of last month, at about 10 p.m., he heard a frantic knocking on the door. When he asked who it was, he was told they were borrowing something. As soon as the door opened, he saw four burly men. One of them, wearing a black Indian silk gown and a box gun hanging on his chest, asked, "Where is the head of this household? Our army lacks funds and needs to borrow 2,000 yuan. Send it to the unit by the fifth day of the month. If you can't raise the money in time, we'll give you ten days, or we'll kill and burn your house to the ground." After hearing this, the farmer was terrified and at a loss of what to do.

川沙 76

Hengsha Flood Disaster Exceptionally Severe: The sixth district under this county (namely Hengsha) is a sea island surrounded by protective embankments to prevent flooding. The Jiangyin Nanqing Academy has a lot of farmland there, so it specially appointed Dai Hanyun as the rent collector. This spring, a water hole was discovered in the outer embankment. The local residents went to the rent collector to request repairs, but Dai ignored them. On the 29th of last month, a sudden typhoon caused the sea water to surge, resulting in the collapse of the embankment. More than ten residents were drowned and more than six thousand mu of fields and houses were turned into swamps. The victims are in a very miserable state, eating in the wind and sleeping in the open. Afterwards, they went to the rent collector to question him. Seeing the unfavorable situation, Dai even resorted to a demonstrative act. The unarmed victims left in disappointment. Now, the district elder, Hu Shaobo, has convened local people to organize a flood relief committee to save the people. On the morning of the 2nd, Xu Mingbo, the police captain sent by the county, and Zhang Zhenpei, a staff member of the Construction Bureau, rushed to the disaster area to investigate everything.

Investigating the Absconding of the Construction Bureau Director: Li Jingzhao, the director of the Construction Bureau of Chuansha County, absconded with public funds on the 16th of last month. The county magistrate, Ruan Kaibao, immediately telegraphed the Provincial Construction Department to report everything and request instructions. On the 31st, the Construction Department sent Yu Dingming, a technical officer, to the county to thoroughly investigate. He finished on the morning of the 1st and took the 2:30 p.m. train from Chuansha back to the province to report.

Zhenjiang 84

Make-Up District Chiefs Will Not Be Made Vacant: The Suzhou Civil Affairs Department stated that the reason for the transfer of district chiefs from various counties to the province for make-up studies was because of their immature abilities or improper actions, and they needed to supplement their academic positions in order to cultivate sound talents. Previously, during the make-up study period, the district chief vacancies in various counties were feared to be without qualified personnel to fill them temporarily, so specific rules for the selection and use of district chiefs were specially formulated to provide relief. According to these rules, the personnel selected are temporarily acting district chiefs. If the members of the transfer province have excellent results after completing the make-up study, they should return to their original districts and continue to work as before. Director Hu specially ordered the county magistrates of various counties not to vacant the district chief positions of those who were transferred to the province for make-up studies. If there are still graduates from the first and second sessions of the district chief training institute in various counties who have not been assigned as district chiefs, they should select the best ones to fill them. If there are not enough, they should be selected in double the number according to the selection and use rules and reported for circle approval.

A Soldier Throws Himself into the River and is Rescued: At noon yesterday, police officer Hu Gongming of the First Branch of the North Riverbank saw a young man commit suicide by throwing himself into the river while on duty at the Ningshao Wharf station. He previously served as a quartermaster's orderly in the First Division of the Thirty-Sixth Army. He became separated while marching in Shandong and went to Shanghai alone. Education News 90

Important News

This Year's Welsh Children's 91

Global Broadcast Answers

The Ministry of Education Issues a Circular Announcing the Answer Contents, Approximately Four Items

The Ministry of Education solicited answers from elementary school children before the global broadcast. In addition to sending four representative works of categories A, B, C, and D to the Welsh Branch, it has now selected the better type A answer and issued it to the education halls and bureaus of various provinces and cities.

The original order of the Ministry of Education was approved by a letter sent by the British Embassy, the secretary of the Welsh Branch of the International Allied Association, as the ninth annual broadcast of the 1930 May 18 global broadcast of children of Zangs. A book titled "Neir Rui in This Year's Global Broadcast of Children" was attached to the Ministry of Education. The Ministry translated the book into Chinese and ordered the educational administrative organs of various provinces and cities to solicit answers from elementary school children and submit them to the Ministry within a time limit. It also replied to each on file. The answer has been received a lot, but there are no provinces and cities where military operations are carried out, and there are also those that have not submitted papers. It is inevitable that the implementation is not strong. The statistical content of the answers submitted in each volume is approximately the following four items:

A. Agree with the good intentions of the original broadcast, but add conditions to the wishes of the League of Nations (such as the organization of the League of Nations should not be dominated by the great powers, but should make all nations equal). B. Agree with the good intentions of the original broadcast, but have doubts about the League of Nations, believing that the League of Nations is dominated by the great powers and cannot truly promote world peace, popular sentiment, and the construction of a better and more beautiful world. C. Both agree with the good intentions of the original broadcast and say that although China is under the invasion of the great powers, it still does not forget the League of Nations and is willing to do its best to help. D. Agree with the good intentions of the original broadcast and are willing to do their best to support the League of Nations. Generally speaking, there is still something to be seen, but ask if there are those who do not know what the League of Nations is or who do not deeply understand the League of Nations. The hall should order elementary school teachers to explain in detail or compile and distribute supplementary teaching materials for reading. In addition to sending four representative works of categories A, B, and D to the British Embassy for forwarding to the Welsh Branch of the International League of Nations Association, a better type A answer and the original broadcast translation are specially selected and attached to the order, and sent to the elementary schools under the jurisdiction to show the children so that they can observe and learn from each other. This order includes a broadcast translation and a type A answer.

Better Answer: One of the answers from Chinese elementary school children to the global radio broadcast from British Welsh children (Type A). Welsh boys and girls, how happy we are to hear your broadcast! This kind of cry is simply "good news." To unite boys and girls from all countries of the world and work hard in each ethnic group to promote world peace, popular sentiment, and create a better and more beautiful world. We sympathize with this very much. Our Chinese nation has always loved peace, and everyone embraces the ambition of a world of great harmony. There is no reason why we should not agree with your wish. However, the current League of Nations is suspected by ordinary small and weak nations. If it can meet the following conditions: (1) Do not take the victorious countries after the war as the main body of the organization, but allow equal participation of famous nations in the world. (2) Do not allow the great powers to manipulate and act as the mouthpiece of the great powers, but seek the universal welfare among all nations. (3) Have the power to make fair judgments on all disputes between the great powers and the small and weak nations. (4) Be able to stop aggression and eliminate all prejudices of powerful nations against small and weak nations. Then we will trust him wholeheartedly and support and help him with all our strength. Welsh children, we fully agree with your good intentions. We are also preparing to help the League of Nations to change the organization as soon as possible and work hard to do practical work in order to gain the faith of the general small and weak nations.

Broadcast Translation: Radio Broadcast Translation of Welsh Children "We, the boys and girls of Wales, England, have come here from valleys or towns to cheer and celebrate with the boys and girls of all countries. Are you, millions of little friends, willing to unite with us today to express gratitude to those who work hard in all nations to build a better and more beautiful world? Are you willing to unite with us in thought, word, and deed, and move forward from now on to build a better and more beautiful world? The League of Nations has opened up this path forward. We should do our best to help the League take on the responsibility of promoting world peace and popular sentiment and move forward."

The arrears have now reached two or three months. The Special Financial Agency owes more than 200,000 yuan. Summer Biology Research Association Work 93

Twenty-four University Professors Attend

Systematic Research on Lancelets

(Special Dispatch from Xiamen, July 25th) The Summer Biology Research Association, jointly organized by Xiamen University and the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, has gathered biology professors from various universities across the country to collaboratively research and deeply explore biological sciences, drawing attention from the scientific community. The association's purpose and methods were previously reported in the news. It is now known that the professors began their work on July 14th. Their various activities are of concern to those in society who are enthusiastic about science. This reporter has made a special trip to Xiamen University to inquire and record the following details:

Attendees: Upon investigation, biology professors from various universities across the country were invited by the Research Association to participate in the research, including: Chen Dafu from Zhongshan University, Hedeman and Miller from Lingnan University, Li Kelo from Northeast University, Liu Chongyue from Peking Union Medical College, Lin Kesheng, Nicholas, Ma Wenzhao, and Hou Xiangchuan, Bo Aili from Yenching University, Huo Bili and Zhu Hairu from Ginling College, Ms. Li Fusi from Ginling Women's College, Liu Jingguo from Qingdao University, Bai Luo from Jiujiang, Yu Kangrong from Shanghai University, Wu Zhaofa from Soochow University, Xu Renjie and Huang Nong from Jinan University, Ma Xu from Zhejiang University, Kellogg from Foochow University, Yuanlai from Gulangyu Yinghua Academy, and Chen Ziying and Lin Shaowen from Xiamen University, totaling twenty-four individuals.

Public Activities: The Research Association held a meeting at 9:00 AM on the 14th, where President Lin Wenqing delivered a welcoming address. Dr. Chen Ziying reported on the preparation process and the significance of the gathering. At 6:00 PM that afternoon, Xiamen University hosted a banquet to welcome the attendees. On the 19th, President Lin Wenqing gave a lecture titled "The Evolution of a Gentleman." On the 20th, participants collected specimens at South Putuo. On the 22nd, they observed lancelets at the Liuwudian fishing factory. These were the activities that had already taken place. Other planned activities include weekly lectures by professors, regular marine specimen collection, a biology and teacher conference on August 9th, a conference on the China Coastal Biology Museum on August 18th, and various banquets and entertainment activities. The closing ceremony is scheduled for August 24th.

Research Topics: The professors will conduct systematic research on the lancelet, a well-known species in biology and a specialty of Xiamen. (1) Lin Kesheng: The nervous and muscular systems of lancelets. (2) Chen Ziying: The respiratory physiology of lancelets. (3) Zhu Hairu: Parasites of lancelets. (4) Yu Kangrong: The diet of lancelets. (5) Hedeman: The habitat of lancelets. In addition, the research topics of other professors include: (6) Liu Chongyue: Marine protozoa. (7) Bo Aili: The distribution of amphibians. (8) Hou Xiangchuan: Capillary management in fish. (9) Ma Wenzhao: The function and physiology of cellular secretion. (10) Nicholas: The phototaxis of water fleas. (11) Huo Bili: The reactivity of parasites. (12) Ms. Li Fusi: Fish in Liuwudian (lancelet production area). (13) Wu Zhaofa: Marine annelids. (14) Xu Renjie: Research on sea urchins. (15) Huang Nong: The development of cricket sperm. (16) Liu Jingguo: Marine biological research. (17) Bai Luo: Echinoderms. (18) Kellogg: Wild bees. (19) Miller: Research on wood-boring mollusks (shipworm). (20) Li Kelo: Research on bamboo. (21) Chen Dafu: Eel research. (22) Ma Xu: The biology of termites. (23) Lin Shaowen: The anatomy of lizards. (24) Da Lai: Details unknown.

The Xiamen Sea Biology reporter learned from most of the professors that the abundance of marine life in the Xiamen sea and the diversity of species are not only the best in the coastal areas of China but also rival those of coastal areas in Europe, America, and Japan that have marine biology museums. For example, the rocky bottoms of South Putuo and the Qidao Islands are like stone basins and mortars, providing habitats for living creatures and forming natural aquariums, mainly producing echinoderms such as sea urchins and starfish. The coastal mudflats of Gulangyu, Heshan, and Xiamen are rich in marine worm-like animals. The Jimei area, due to the confluence of tides from the left and right ports, produces even richer and more diverse animals. The lancelets of Liuwudian are world-renowned. Therefore, Xiamen is truly a unique and excellent environment for studying biology. As for the marine biology museum, all the professors are enthusiastic about it, and positive results are expected after the meeting.

Overview of Facilities: The reporter finally visited the facilities of the research institute, which is the biology department of Xiamen University. The northwestern rooms on the first floor are specimen display areas, with abundant materials from marine life to mammals, mostly collected over the years by Dr. Bing Zhi and Professor Laide. Most of the fish, birds, and shellfish have been identified, thanks to the painstaking work of Dr. Bing. The whale, porpoise, and sea cow specimens are particularly rare. The abundance of specimens provides for various specialized research. The southeastern side of the biology department consists of experimental laboratories, with two large rooms, three medium rooms, and three small rooms. Water pipes have been installed, and all rooms have access to flowing seawater, allowing marine organisms to be kept indoors for live research. The experimental equipment is complete. The second floor houses the biology library and the biological material supply center. The basement has storage rooms. The biological material supply center aims to provide biological specimens to universities and middle schools. Many schools have already placed orders, which greatly helps in the development of biological science education in China. ○ The Beijing Summer Education Research Association Holds a Meeting.

The Beijing Education Bureau's Summer Education Research Association held meetings from the 1st to the 14th, lasting for two weeks. Meetings were held daily from 8:00 AM to 10:00 AM to discuss Party principles, school administration, kindergarten teaching, natural education, testing and statistics, phonetic symbols, and textbook review in seven groups. From 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM, famous figures were invited to give public lectures. The association held an opening ceremony at 8:00 AM on the 1st at the Central District Experimental School. Several hundred teachers and staff from primary and secondary schools across the city attended. Liu Xuzhou of the Education Bureau reported on the purpose of the meeting. A representative from the Municipal Party Committee gave a speech on the need for research to improve education and the importance of research for teachers. Peng Linxian discussed the history and necessity of phonetic symbols. Subsequently, the seven groups were divided and held separate discussions. Each group elected two or three chairpersons and secretaries. The meetings adjourned around 10:00 AM. Xia Zhanchu from the School Education Section of the Bureau went to the Ministry of Education that day and has contacted Vice Minister Zhu Jingnong and Director Gu Shusen to attend the meetings and give lectures on different days.

Local News

Municipal Summer School Holds Closing Ceremony Yesterday 94

The first session of the summer school organized by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau has been running for three weeks. The closing ceremony was held yesterday (the 2nd) at 9:30 AM. Director Chen, Secretary Ni, and over two hundred students attended the ceremony. After the ceremony, the principal gave a report, and Director Chen delivered a speech: "Today is the closing ceremony of the summer school. Before the report, let us observe three minutes of silence to mourn the passing of Ms. Xia Bao'ying, a teacher from Wusong Peiji Primary School." After the silence, he continued, "This summer school lasted only three weeks, but many lectures were given during these three weeks. The school authorities put a lot of thought into hiring lecturers, and the lecturers enthusiastically explained the material. We should thank them for that. In the past, summer sessions included training courses and workshops, but they suffered from common problems, such as the freedom to attend or not attend as one pleased. The summer school aims to avoid these problems. This is the first session, and future sessions will continue to be organized according to the continuing education regulations. A total of 360 people registered for this session. Seventy-five people never attended any classes. Among those who chose the Party Principles course, 66 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 20 people did not attend any classes, and 30 people had perfect attendance. For the Design and Teaching Methods course, 179 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 52 people did not attend any classes, and 77 people had perfect attendance. For the Work Course, 148 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 33 people did not attend any classes, and 60 people had perfect attendance. For Elementary School Organization and Administration, 141 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 39 people did not attend any classes, and 60 people had perfect attendance. For Special Children's Psychology, 112 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 48 people did not attend any classes, and 35 people had perfect attendance. For Educational Testing and Statistics, 153 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, 34 people did not attend any classes, and 44 people had perfect attendance. For Health Education, 56 people were absent for more than one-third of the classes, and 22 people did not attend any classes, with 10 people having perfect attendance. As for the required courses, 360 people registered, 75 people did not attend any classes, and 39 people had perfect attendance. These statistics are disappointing. All courses are important, but only a few people had perfect attendance. This shows that elementary school teachers in the city hold a perfunctory attitude towards education. However, these statistics may not be entirely accurate, as there may be special circumstances, such as illness due to the hot weather. The reasons for absence should be investigated to obtain more accurate statistics. Among the students in the required courses, there were 66 current principals, 77 class teachers, 44 teachers, 17 subject teachers, and 1 kindergarten director from municipal schools. There were also 4 principals, 2 class teachers, 2 academic affairs directors, and 16 teachers from private schools, totaling 24 people. This is also noteworthy. The regulations for continuing education for teachers and staff are being revised, but the established principle is that all teachers should have the opportunity to attend summer school for continuing education. Therefore, absence from summer school without reason is not allowed. Continuing education is for one's own benefit and cannot be limited by law. Elementary school teachers should seize every opportunity to improve themselves and acquire new knowledge, skills, and methods to impart to children in the future. They should realize that attending summer school is a good method of continuing education, a right, not an obligation, an opportunity, not a responsibility. Please note this and inform your colleagues." Next,

Teachers and staff gave speeches. Tang Shouqian briefly stated that this summer school is to promote self-cultivation. Teachers have a very important responsibility, and self-cultivation is essential to fulfill their mission. Summer school is an opportunity for self-cultivation and can solve various difficult problems. Secretary Ni then gave a speech with three points for consideration: (1) China did not have new education in the past, and we should strive for it now. (2) We should recognize that we are ordinary people. (3) We should pay attention to students' physical well-being and also take care of our own bodies. Finally, a student representative gave a reply, thanking the lecturers for their enthusiastic guidance and hoping that the spirit of these three weeks will continue to guide them. The ceremony ended with the dispersal of attendees.

Liaoning Province Selects Physical Education Students for Overseas Study 101

Two to Study Abroad, Three Domestically

Panyang Correspondent: Zhang Hanqing previously donated 5 million yuan to the Liaoning Province Primary and Secondary School Education Fund. The education association and other organizations have formed a fund management committee and decided on a distribution plan, including the selection of physical education students for overseas study. It has been decided to implement this plan after the summer vacation this year. Five students will be selected, one to study in the Americas with an annual fee of 5,600 yuan in national currency, one to study in Japan with an annual fee of 2,500 yuan in national currency, and three to study domestically with an annual fee of 500 yuan each in national currency. The study period is set for two years, and the scholarships will be renewed upon expiration. The board of directors has entrusted the Department of Education to handle all matters related to the selection, and registration will begin on July 24th and end on August 10th. The examination will be held on August 12th. The registration procedures include submitting a graduation certificate and a 4.5-inch half-length photo, and completing a guarantee and application form. The qualifications for applying are that those studying abroad must have graduated from a public vocational school or higher, and those studying domestically must have graduated from a public or registered private high school or higher. However, their place of origin must be the three northeastern provinces. The examination will be held in three stages, with strict rules that those who fail the first examination cannot participate in the second examination, and those who fail the second examination cannot participate in the third examination. The examination subjects and standards are as follows: (A) Overseas Study: The first examination consists of one item: a physical examination (1) physical examination, (2) medical examination. The second examination consists of five items: Party Principles, Chinese Language (Classical), Foreign Language (English for those going to the United States, Japanese for those going to Japan, with a supplemental English test), based on high school entrance level, Outline of Education, Mathematics (Algebra, Geometry, Trigonometry), Psychology, Biology, Physiology, Hygiene, Physical Chemistry, and Physical Education Knowledge (Brief History of Chinese Physical Education, Physical Education Equipment, Sports Rules, Judging Knowledge). Physical Fitness Test (1) Athletics: Five events, 100 meters in 14 seconds, 1500 meters in 6 minutes, 12-pound shot put 30 feet, high jump 4 feet 5 inches, long jump 15 feet. (2) Physical Strength Test: Five events, pull-ups 8 times, arm extensions and flexions 8 times, vault over 4 feet 4 inches, rope climbing once, average of four sports. (3) Ball Skills: Five types: soccer, basketball, tennis, team ball, baseball. (4) Swimming: Those who have studied swimming will be tested, but it will not be counted in the score. Those who have not studied swimming must practice in advance before going abroad if they are admitted. The third examination is an oral examination. (B) Domestic Study: The examination is divided into three stages, the same as for overseas study. The first examination is exactly the same as for overseas study. The second examination consists of Party Principles, Chinese Language (Classical), English Language, Mathematics (Algebra, Geometry, Trigonometry), Biology, Physiology, Hygiene, Physical Chemistry, Chinese and Foreign History and Geography, and Physical Fitness Test (1) Athletics: Choose two events. (2) Ball Skills: Choose two types. The third examination is the same as for overseas study. (Wanhua, 22nd)

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter Hai Ke

A: Your gold watch was stolen by a thief, how come you are still wearing it today? Is it a new one?

B: No, it's the original one. Because the thief was very stupid, he broke the spring. It wasn't worth it for him to repair it, so he sent it back.

A: That old gentleman's head of red hair is really funny. From afar, it looks like a ball of fire. B: I say it looks like a red sun. So the other day, he went home late at night, and the roosters on both sides of the neighbors thought it was the rising sun and crowed together. Do you think it's funny or not? A: My father had a joke the other day. It's very funny to tell.

B: Then why don't you tell it to me so I can laugh?

A: You know how nearsighted my father is. The other day, he walked by the field and bumped into a cow. He quickly apologized and said, "Sorry, madam." He looked closely and saw that it was a cow. He was very ashamed and left. Not far away, he bumped into a woman. He thought it was still the cow and scolded, "You animal, is it you again?" He was slapped twice by the woman. Do you think it's funny or not?

A: Recently, cases of suicide have emerged endlessly. What prevention methods do you think can be taken to avoid a decrease in population?

B: I think people who commit suicide should be treated the same as murderers. Beheading or shooting is acceptable.

A Short Stay at Mogan Mountain (2) Jing Bo 103

The car arrived at Yucun before 8 o'clock. Mogan Mountain was already visible in the distance. After getting off the car, the Highway Bureau sent someone to have the passengers fill out a survey form. Items such as name, occupation, address, and date of arrival and departure must be written. Western tourists must present their passports before being allowed to climb the mountain, which is not as free as in previous years. The number of residents in the mountain, both Chinese and foreign, is no less than several hundred. They live in harmony with each other, and theft has never occurred. The Mogan Mountain Administration Bureau investigates residents very carefully, and the people in the mountain know the foreign tourists very well. It is easy to know who is staying in a hotel and who is renting a house at first glance, so thieves have nowhere to hide. The Highway Bureau's strict investigation also has an impact on the safety of the mountain.

Mountain sedan chairs are also managed by the Highway Bureau. The number of chair carriers depends on the passenger's weight. There are even those who need eight people to carry them. Each person is paid 7 corners, and tickets are purchased in advance at Yucun. The chair carriers bicker beside them, trying to solicit the strongest passengers, just like the situation of the Roman human market, which is very funny. There are two ways to climb the mountain. The old road, Wukang Road, has steep stone steps and is not easy to climb, but the route is shorter. Most chair carriers take this route. However, at the precipice, it is best to abandon the chair and walk to ensure safety. The new road, Mogan Mountain Road, is owned by the Highway Bureau and is relatively flat. Due to the shape of the mountain, it spirals down, with winding paths and ingenious architecture. However, the journey is slightly longer than the old road. Travelers may want to take the new road for stability. Recently, someone suggested that the authorities expand the new road, leveling the steep parts and raising the low parts, so that cars can pass. In my opinion, the new road does have the possibility of being rebuilt into a car road. When it is realized in the future, wouldn't it be more convenient for mountain climbers?

Mogan Mountain was initially within the sphere of influence of Westerners. The Summer Resort Association managed everything, and Chinese were not allowed to join the association. All the ball fields, swimming pools, etc. were closed to Chinese. The Shanghai Bank had a summer office in the mountain. Its manager, Mr. Li Zhenfu, a righteous and promising young man, vigorously fought against the Summer Resort Association, explaining the great righteousness. The Westerners were overwhelmed and invited the Chinese to join the association. All the ball fields and swimming pools were opened to all. This was praised by those who heard about it. However, this was still during the warlord era. After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, the Zhejiang Provincial Government was established and resolutely established the Mogan Mountain Administration Bureau. The director, Mr. Lin Biao, believed that Westerners were protected by China and should pay taxes within Chinese territory. He consulted with Mr. Li Zhenfu. Mr. Li drafted a notice in Western language and posted it on the main street, stating that those who resisted taxes would have their residences sealed. He then sent people to deliver the notice to each household for signing. The Westerners had no way to avoid it, so they complied with the regulations and paid taxes. However, they were unwilling and sent letters to Western newspapers to forcefully criticize the Chinese, but they did not dare to sign their names. Mr. Li also wrote a long article to refute it. Now, the arrogance of the Westerners has subsided greatly. The responsibility of society lies in advising the meritorious. Mr. Li's efforts to fight for sovereignty cannot be overstated.

○ Briand's Signing Creates New Record Planning

French Foreign Minister Aristide Briand has signed as many as 236 treaties on behalf of France with various countries, creating a new record in diplomatic history for signing treaties. The most amazing thing is the short amount of time he has been at it. Now he is continuing his duty to make treaties.

It is found that the first treaty signed by Briand was less than ten years ago. The treaty was a distribution of miners' gratuity between France and Belgium. Followed by the Angola Treaty in October 1921 and the Washington Treaty in December of the same year, which were all related to Pacific affairs. Since then, all French international conventions have been signed by Briand, such as the Dawes and Young Plans, but all in the name of France, with Briand as the representative. As for the treaties signed in Briand's personal name, only the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The official name of the treaty is still the Paris Treaty, not in his personal name. Treaties for the happiness of mankind

Including international restrictions on the arms trade and the use of poisonous gas.

His advocacy of peace and the elimination of war is particularly admirable. Since becoming Foreign Minister, Briand has concluded arbitration and friendship treaties with various countries, including Spain, Portugal, Turkey, Finland, Holland, the United States, Denmark, Poland, and Yugoslavia. Only Germany and Russia have not yet had hope of reaching an agreement.

A Short Record of Spending the Summer in Jiang Village by Chen Boying 104

My friend, Mr. Gu Zhizhou, lives in a place called Jiabin, which is twenty li away from Qingpu County town. We have made several appointments, but I have been entangled in worldly affairs and have not been able to fulfill them. This year, I finally got leave during the summer vacation and went to visit him. Although it was a journey of a hundred li, I experienced the rumbling of wheels, the sound of water in the boat cabin, and the feelings of a traveler. His house faces south and faces the river. Several large elm trees in front of the gate, with their branches and leaves spreading out, block the sunlight from reaching the ground. Across the river are thousands of acres of flat fields, a boundless expanse of green, dotted with woods. Two mountains can be seen in the distance, called Ji Mountain and Yun Mountain, which are where the Lu brothers, Shilu Heng and Shilong Yun, studied. The mountains are small and not high. Slightly to the east is She Mountain, where the red walls of a church can be vaguely seen. Compared to Ji Mountain, She Mountain is like a great sorcerer. The house has three courtyards and five rooms. In the back is a courtyard planted with cypress trees and yellow gardenias, among other plants. Outside the wall are many bamboo trees, which make a rustling sound in the wind, arousing thoughts of autumn. The villagers live together in groups. Behind each house, bamboo and trees are planted, concealing the village from outsiders. Mr. Gu told me that in past years, during the wars in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, when soldiers passed through, they saw the dense trees and bamboo forests and thought there were no inhabitants, so they did not bother to come in, thus avoiding disaster. This is thanks to the bamboo. Outside the bamboo are fields with crisscrossing paths, ending only at the river, which embraces the village on three sides. In the morning, I walk the fields. The sun is just rising, and the heat is not scorching, but the dew is heavy, soaking my shoes and socks. After returning, I take a book and read it at the gate. From time to time, a long wind crosses the river, scattering the branches of the trees and fluttering my sleeves. My whole body feels comfortable, and I have the feeling of discarding the throne and facing south as king. At midday, the clouds do not move, and the sunlight is very strong. The cicada's chirping is like boiling water. I then break a melon and eat it. When I am a little tired, I lean on the couch and take a nap. When I wake up, I ask for a chessboard and play a game of chess. Mr. Gu is more skilled than I, but he does not fully exert his skill. When the game ends, the sun is already setting, no longer something to fear but something to be intimate with, like a high official who, once retired, loses all his former power and influence. Then I go out for a leisurely walk in the village. The evening breeze brushes past me from time to time. The sound of cicadas is slightly tired, and the sound of well sweeps begins, and the croaking of frogs can also be heard here and there. The water birds and partridges in the distant trees also call, though they call to tell of a clear sky tomorrow. Behind the distant trees, the evening glow is beautiful like a painting, with five colors intertwined indescribably. When the glow disappears, the moon rises. When the moon rises, it seems to be suppressed, struggling to rise. It first shows its edge, then gradually half of it, and then gradually the whole thing. Its color is like fire, and it is quite large. The higher it rises, the smaller and whiter it becomes. When it no longer shrinks, it is already three or four times smaller than when it first rose. After dinner, I drag a wicker chair and sit under the tree, listening to the old villagers tell ghost stories. Although they are absurd, they are still enjoyable. In this way, I spent a week, drinking wine, with the host and guests not urging each other to drink, stopping when they were satisfied. We also played bamboo war games, no longer remembering who won or lost. Every meal included crabs, which, although not fully grown, were incredibly tender, unlike anything found elsewhere. I was pressed by affairs and regretted how quickly this week passed.

Thoughts on a Trip to the East (20) (2) 105

Qian Hua

Unexpectedly, one wave of incidents involving Filipino athletes had not subsided when another arose. On the 31st, a theft occurred at the Japan Youth Hall, where a Filipino boxer stole money from the dormitory of a Japanese athlete.
