The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the sky in the Yangtze River basin was cloudy, and the seasonal wind was quite strong in the southeast coastal areas of the country. There was a low pressure area between the Ryukyu Islands and the Ogasawara Islands. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 93.2 and the lowest was 79.2. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 91.0 and the lowest was 73.4.

Incoming Correspondence

Preliminary Issues in Aiding the People's Food Supply 189

China is vast in territory, densely populated, and rich in resources. Since ancient times, agriculture has been the foundation of the country, with about 70% to 80% of the population engaged in agriculture. In the past, when agriculture in Europe, America, and Japan had not yet reached full development, China's exports of agricultural products were very large. In modern times, due to the development of science and the dedication to research and improvement, agriculture in various countries has flourished and progressed rapidly. Looking back at China, not only has there been no progress in thousands of years, but it has also declined daily. Even the most important food staples for people's livelihood, such as rice, wheat, and flour, still rely on foreign countries. Other minor agricultural products have seen even greater declines in production. According to customs reports, rice imported from Saigon, Ceylon, and other places reaches more than ten million yuan per year. If such a huge leak is not remedied, its impact on the national economy and people's livelihood will be very serious. China's land area and population are ten or a hundred times greater than other countries. Why is there no panic of food shortages in other countries, while China, which claims to be an agricultural advanced nation, has such backward production? This is a value for extensive study. The reason for the development of agriculture in Europe, America, and Japan is due to material civilization, which China does not have. Another major reason is that farmers can use scientific methods to improve agriculture. We have learned from the rapid advances in agriculture in Europe, America, and Japan that in this age of scientific prosperity, stagnation will lead to elimination. Without actively improving to seek production development, there is no way to solve all the difficulties of people's livelihood. However, the path to improvement has myriad aspects and cannot be achieved overnight. Where should we start? The only way is to choose what is easy and quick to take effect and start first, which is to improve fertilizer. The fertilizers used by Chinese farmers to cultivate crops are soybeans, animal manure, river mud, and grass ash. However, the most important nutrients for plants, nitrogen, phosphorus, and potassium, are mostly insufficient in these fertilizers, which affects the prosperity of plants and the harvest. Agricultural experts in various countries know that these fertilizers cannot obtain a full harvest, so they have conducted precise research and invented chemical fertilizers (i.e., fertilizer powder) to supplement the deficiencies of natural fertilizers. The effect is grand, the procedure is simple, and it is very economical. If it is combined with soybeans, the effect is even greater. Therefore, fertilizer powder occupies an extremely important position in agriculture today and is recognized as the only essential product for increasing production. Foreign farmers have used it for a long time with remarkable results. The abundance of agricultural products in various countries today must be attributed to fertilizer powder. It is a pity that Chinese farmers pay little attention to it. China's population was claimed to be 400 million several years ago. With years of reproduction, the increase in population has exceeded this number. On the one hand, the population is increasing daily, and on the other hand, production should also increase to avoid supply exceeding demand, and life will not feel any hardship. But now we only see the daily increase in population and do not see the increase in production. With more needs and insufficient supply, there is a panic of food shortages. The current unstable state of society and the rice price rising to more than twenty yuan per stone make people across the country feel the pain of living hard, which is due to the fundamental reduction in production. If we do not vigorously develop the production aspect at this time, not only will the problem of food shortages not be solved, but the national economy and social peace will also be greatly affected. Lion Horse Brand Fertilizer Powder is a famous German specialty with excellent quality and great effectiveness. If it is used together with domestic natural fertilizers to cultivate various crops, they will be prosperous and fruitful. This fertilizer powder has been inspected and certified by the Agricultural Products Inspection Institute of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, and is recognized as beneficial to agricultural crops and harmless to the soil. Now that production is decreasing and there is a domestic food shortage, I hope that my comrades in the agricultural field will rise up and advocate the use of this fertilizer powder to increase production and relieve food shortages. This is the task at hand.

School Life 194

In the modern trend, all new developments in civilization, no matter which aspect, are centered on cities. The only city in China is Shanghai. In terms of culture, Shanghai should be the birthplace of national culture. Just looking at the various publications that spring up like bamboo shoots after rain can represent this. Especially in recent years, the craze for illustrated publications. Not to mention anything else, even the old Shen Bao, like Old Master Q, has responded to the trend and published Illustrated Shen Bao. Xinwen Bao is of course not to be outdone. Other newspapers may not be able to achieve this goal temporarily due to economic reasons, but they do not necessarily lack this hope. As for the publication of illustrated magazines, there are even more of them. In the modern trend of civilization, publications without pictures seem unable to represent the spirit of the times. To put it a bit too strongly, it seems a bit outdated and backward. Readers, I hope you can believe it. We only need to pay attention to the publications that our young people read, and it is not difficult to prove. If you don't believe me, let's try to go into the dormitories of various universities and visit them. In addition to textbooks, reference books, and books that are rich in research, various illustrated magazines and various pictorials have almost become essential pastimes. "If our young people don't open literary publications or picture publications to read, then the life they live will be too boring.

Among the various illustrated publications, I love to read two kinds. One is the "School Life" that I am introducing today, and the other is "White Goose." I will introduce the latter at another time. Now I will only talk briefly about the former. She is a weekly publication. She has been produced for nine issues. What does she look like beautifully? How rich is the content? How sophisticated is the printing? How exquisite is the binding? Fortunately, there is evidence, so I don't need to be long-winded. What I want to introduce is the recently published ninth issue.

I don't just love the four-color plate cover photo. I love the words "School Life" and "schooILife" in white letters with blue borders, set against a silver background, which are "bright and eye-catching", making people feel a poetic beauty at first sight. An extremely beautiful color plate photo of Ms. Liu Liuying of Guanghua University. This photo is excellent. The rose and black colors are set off. I dare to say that not many of the color plates in Shanghai's various picture publications can surpass her. Here, a question worthy of study arises. The editors of this publication must have sufficient knowledge of art. Mr. Ji Xiaobo, the editor of this publication, is a painter, so the printing of "School Life" can surpass others.

This issue's cover features several photos of Ms. Chen Yuejun in various poses, most of which are full of enthusiasm and can be used as a reference for a group of ladies who love to take pictures. There is also a photo of "Female Poet Yu Xiuyun Visiting Tin," which is quite poetic and worthy of being a female poet's photo. In terms of illustrations, such as human body art, color plates, and humorous satirical paintings, they are all very eye-catching. Let's talk about the text.

The graduation song on the first page is necessary to introduce. Not only is the combination of Chinese and Western characters clever, but it is also timely. Isn't it the summer vacation now? Graduating students must like it very much after hearing it. Listen to it.

Everyone, don't be depressed. Please drink iced soda and sing the happy graduation song below.

Dean of Students and Empress of Datong University 195

Datong University, which rents houses and relies on loans for food, has, through the efforts of founder Ou Yuanhuai and the students of the school, in the spirit of cooperation between teachers and students, built new school buildings on Fanwangdu, such as Qunxian Hall, Qunce Zhai, Qunli Zhai, and Qunying Zhai. The buildings are magnificent and magnificent. Although the equipment in the material aspect cannot be said to be above all universities in the country, it can also be comparable. It has the model of the highest institution of learning, and other facilities such as the library are being expanded, and the science museum and gymnasium are also being planned. The number of students is expected to be more than 1,500 in the next semester. The gathering of heroes can be described as a grand event. In addition to the sporadic disclosures of the school's news in various newspapers, the problem of the school's dean of students and the empress is of great concern to the general students. It is learned that Mr. Zhu Zhangbao, the dean of students of the school, is good at eloquence and communication, and is very modest in dealing with people. Since taking office, teachers and students have been at peace, and any disputes have been resolved easily. Now, due to various problems, he suddenly resigned. Although the school affairs meeting decided to retain him and President Ou sincerely persuaded him, Mr. Zhu insisted on resigning because he was hired by the Faculty of Law and Politics (as the dean of students). However, the students of the school speculate on the selection of his successor. According to reliable information, there is a rumor that Mr. Yu Zhihan, the director of the school's preparatory course, will take on the role concurrently. As for the empress problem, because the school's girls' dormitory was originally in West Shanghai, it has long been known as the West Palace (opposite Fudan's East Palace). Although the empress's selection has not been formally voted on in the past, all the students have generally recognized Ms. Zhang Yuanhe. Ms. Zhang has graduated during the summer vacation and is preparing to go to the United States next spring. Therefore, the empress problem in the next semester has become a topic of discussion among the school's students. It is heard that Yu Xiuyun, a new student who was admitted to this year's first year, is the granddaughter of Mr. Yu Qiaqing. Ms. Yu graduated from the Patriotic Girls' School this summer. Ms. Yu's appearance is extremely beautiful in the East, and the new literature has long been famous at sea. I met a member of the school's student union who stayed at the school yesterday and asked about the two matters. According to him, there is indeed a saying that Yu Zhihan is the dean of students. Mr. Yu has no ill will towards the students, but he is not very close and is not a party member. It is difficult to predict whether it will be determined in the future. As for the empress problem, the female students will be very enthusiastic in the next semester, and there will be no lack of candidates (because there is now a saying in the school that the summer school is prosperous and the female students are flourishing). Although the students have long admired Ms. Yu's noble style, they have no chance to meet her. Therefore, whether she can be elected must depend on her attitude towards the students before a decision can be made. I would like to offer what I have learned to the readers, and I think it will be a pleasure to hear it. (Xiangmin)

Chinese Student Wins American Poetry Prize 196

The "Los Angeles Times" of the United States holds a literary award essay contest every year to reward contributors. This year, Mr. Lee Sbippey, the editor of the poetry section of the newspaper, specially reviewed the works published in the section and rigorously selected from 600 submissions. The first prize was awarded to Zhao Yuanzhang, a Chinese student. The others were novelists, veterans, and police officers. Zhao Yuanzhang's poem has an atmosphere of the American mystery writer Edgar Allan Poe, which was highly appreciated by the editor. However, the poem begins with himself sitting alone in a room dreaming with a sad tone, and ends with "the wind brings me the flowers of death", which seems to be a groan that Chinese youth should not be uttering in a foreign country. (Yi Kang)

Xinjiang Snapshots

Xinjiang is located on the frontier, with abundant resources, a mild climate, and a peaceful order, free from the disasters of war. Its people enjoy a life of peace. The land is coveted by England and Russia, and internal strife is endless. This pure land has not yet enjoyed a moment of peace. From the Han and Tang Dynasties, there were connections with the Western Regions. The Qing Dynasty suppressed the Hui people, not hesitating to waste manpower and resources, because Xinjiang is not only a defensive perimeter, but also related to the overall situation of Europe and Asia. This spring, Zhu Xiting, the secretary of the Xinjiang Provincial Education Department and director of the Tonghua Library, traveled to the Pingjin, Shanghai, and Hangzhou areas for several months. After that, he spent four months in the desert taking photographs. He has now safely returned to his hometown. Many photos have been sent. Here are some important ones. It is hoped that those who feel responsible for the rise and fall of the nation will take note of these preparations. (Zhang Jianbai)

(1) Sheep Herds: Although Xinjiang was once the ancient homeland of the Xiongnu, and is now regarded as a border region of the country, the residents are engaged in both agriculture and animal husbandry. In the northern regions of Yili and Tacheng, the situation is such that the Kyrgyz, Bulut and other tribes are nomadic people who live by moving according to water and grass. Even in the areas near Bortala, although they are engaged in both agriculture and animal husbandry, they are more inclined towards animal husbandry. Therefore, most people in Xinjiang, except for a small number of Han people living in the upper classes, rely on animal husbandry for clothing and food. This has remained unchanged since ancient times. The area is located in the Kunlun Mountains, the source of ten thousand waters. Looking out over the vast plains and green grass, it is a natural pasture. In the past, the profits from agriculture in Xinjiang Province were said to be several times higher than those of other provinces, but the profits from animal husbandry are even several times higher than those of agriculture. This is indeed not an exaggeration.

(2) Fur Clothing for Travel: When traveling to Xinjiang, it is necessary to wear fur clothing and hats as the weather gradually changes when traveling west. Otherwise, it will be impossible to withstand the cold. Photo by Zhu Xiting.

(3) Transportation: Xinjiang is located on the extreme border, compounded by the obstruction of water, mountains, deserts, and quicksand. Therefore, transportation is extremely difficult and time-consuming, unparalleled even in a journey around the world. Moreover, the benefits of boats and trains are useless. One can only rely on horses and mule carts for transportation. The only animal that can bear heavy loads and travel long distances is the camel. The progress of society and the development of civilization are greatly influenced by transportation.

(4) Camel Shade: Who is traveling in the desert, seeking shade?

(5) Agriculture: Farms extend over 20,000 li, nearly four times the size of Sichuan, and several times larger than Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Thirty to forty percent of the land consists of towering mountains and valleys. The remaining area is vast wilderness with abundant water and grass. Even without rain, the land is fertile and the climate is moderate. The northern region is comparable to the Tianjin area, while the climate in the two regions is temperate, making them suitable for agriculture like the regions south of the Yangtze River. Currently, only over 13 million mu of land are cultivated, mainly producing wheat, barley, and sorghum, followed by rice. The photo above shows the Dihua North Agricultural Experiment Station, introducing scientific farming methods. Hong Yongwu, a former Tuntian official in Turpan and Kashgar, also introduced agricultural benefits.

(6) Jade Tablet: The tablet is located outside the north gate of Zhenxi City. It was built in the second year of the Han Dynasty's Heping era and is of great historical value.

(7) Fishing: Bosten Lake is the largest lake in the southern part of Xinjiang Province. People use dugout canoes to fish in it.

(8) Gathering Firewood: Travelers gather firewood in the wilderness to prepare meals.

(9) Forests: Xinjiang is located on a high plateau with undulating mountains and dense forests. The Tianshan Mountains stretch for over a thousand li from Qitai to Barkol in the north, covered entirely with pine and fir trees. The Mingduo Wannian Pine and the Barluk Mountains of Tacheng extend for over two hundred li, filled with pines and firs. The shade of the Kunlun Mountains is also covered with pine, elm, and poplar trees. Although nature is generous, human efforts are lacking. In Yili and Tacheng, which are close to Russia, the logging has been going on for ten years with no regard for restrictions. Recently, a timber company has been established in an attempt to control logging, but due to insufficient capital and inconvenient transportation, the results are poor. This picture shows a glimpse of the Tianshan forests.

(9) Ms. Lu Erzhao, a student at McTyeire School, is scheduled to go to the United States on August 16th to study literature at Williams College. (Zhu Shaoping)

(10) The wife and son of Mr. Shen Nengbo, a member of the Northeast Cultural Society.

(1) Mr. Wang Jingwei arrived in Tianjin from Hong Kong on July 23rd. This is a picture of him leaving the city government. To Mr. Wang's left is Mr. Gu Mengyu, and to his right are Mayor Wang Faqin, Cui Tingxian, and Mr. Zeng Zhongming, Mr. Wang's secretary.

(2) Mr. Wang Jingwei transferred to a plane to Shanghai from a boat from Japan when he arrived in Tianjin. The picture shows his arrival at the shore.

(3) Mr. Lü Di, Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government and Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Eighth Route Army of the National Revolutionary Army, passed away on June 15th in Guangzhou. He was reburied in the Zhongda Hospital on July 15th.

(4) The left corner shows a portrait of Mr. Lü Di (Wu Qianli Photo Agency)

(5) The Hankou General Chamber of Commerce protested against the soaring rice prices and the increasingly difficult lives of ordinary people. The photo shows the scene of a price reduction appeal from 6:00 AM to 10:00 AM. There were many petitioners. (Zhu Yunshan)

(6) The front view of the Zhongshan Mausoleum under construction. The ship will be launched on the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's death this year. (Ye Yangmin)

(7) The rickshaw pullers of Qingdao went on strike on July 21st due to price increases by the owners. This photo shows the scene of over a thousand rickshaw pullers petitioning at the Public Security Bureau the next day.

(8) The China Physical Education School, which was established four years before the Republic of China and suspended three years ago, has been renamed the China Physical Education School after the Alumni Association was restored. Mr. Lai is the principal. This photo shows the first board meeting.

(9) The Shanghai Education Bureau held an exhibition of school supplies at the Fourth Chengzhi Primary School and Qicheng Primary School from July 24th for three days. The exhibits were divided into teaching materials, recreational equipment, examination supplies, etc., to promote the improvement of school facilities.

(10) Mr. Lu Dianyang, the chairman of the meeting, is reporting on the association's affairs at the first annual meeting of the Chinese Children's Welfare Association held in Shanghai.
